Poland Focus Tree
The Emergency Session
In a Speech to the Sejm, the King has put pressure on its members to resolve the crisis quickly, lest he make good on his threat to use his significant powers to resolve the issues plaguing the nation as he sees fit. The Sejm will begin working to pull Poland out from the crisis, while in the background the King will begin deciding whether he feels the parliament can really be trusted to do what he asks of them.
Strengthen the Interpartisan Circle
Compromising with Polish liberals through concessions may be an unpopular choice to some in court, but it is a far better option for maintaining popularity and long-term stability going forward. Through reinforcing the influence of the moderate \
Empower Provincial Assemblies
Poland has long had a system of regional assemblies, known as Sejmiki, which have survived throughout the nation's long and turbulent history. The power of the Sejmiki fluctuated depending on the strength of the central government, and their competencies can often vary between regions. By empowering these assemblies, we can help our citizens feel engaged in local decision making, being more inclined to take their grievances through moderate institutional means.
Concessions to the Unions
The crash resulting from Black Monday has shown that there are flaws in our economy: the insecurity and misery brought about by economic decline has led to many seeing these flaws as an indictment of traditional politics, leading them to be seduced by the siren's song from Paris. While we may disagree with syndicalists in almost every way, making minor reforms on policy areas such as workers' rights and welfare would go a long way in keeping the average worker on our side.
Form the Königstreue
King August has always surrounded himself with a significant number of advisors, many of whom represent the interests of German business and social leaders. These figures have long been pushing to have their place at the King's ear institutionalised, to protect their position going forward. While this decision will not be popular among Poles left on the outside, they have promised certain kickbacks in return for support from the Palace which is desperately needed in these times.
Work with the Elites
Now that the position of the King's closest advisors has been entrenched, they have begun to make further \
Royal Tours
An unfortunate side effect of the King choosing to elevate many Germans into an entrenched position of power, is a growing feeling among the populace that the monarchy is far more concerned with representing German interests than Polish ones. In a bid to assuage these sentiments, the King's staff have drawn up a significant list of itineraries of tours and details of patronages which will serve to win the Palace a lot of goodwill with the average citizen.
Direction of the Privy Council
Now that the King has begun shaping the makeup of his inner circle, attention has begun to focus itself on the Privy Council. This body, composed of a mixture of German and Polish members, has an extremely close relationship with the King and plays a big part in fostering the ties between the Palace and different groups. The King will have to carefully decide who he wishes to appoint to his council, as it will be difficult to balance the demands of the Germans and Poles.
Foster Polish-German Ties
While the King's efforts to win the support of powerful German interests have begun to pay some dividends, many of his advisors are now calling for him to deepen the ties even further, firmly placing the Polish nation into the German fold. They are certain that they can convince their contacts in Berlin to make significant investments in the nation's economy, provided the King makes it clear he is a firm friend of Berlin.
Guarantee the Holdings of Landowners
While making some compromises with leftist groups has spooked many wealthy individuals in the nation, the King wishes to make it clear that such steps in no way mean that there are any plans afoot to dismantle large rural interests. The Palace plans to do this by creating legal safeguards against what they call \
Address the Land Issue
While almost no one in the government wishes to see the kind of land robbery the Centrolew is speaking of, there's much to improve in our current situation. There are many estates which are ran very inefficiently, and also many which are too small to be truly productive. By rationalising land usage we should be able to improve the productiveness of Polish agriculture.
A Weapon against the Underground
There has always been suspicion that shadowy organisations wield a significant amount of power within the nation, but the exact scale of this has always been a mystery. It is because of this that we have embarked on the expansion of our domestic intelligence services in order to finally root out the underground schemers.
Rein in the Sejm
While some form of communication between the people and the King can be good, the Sejm has enjoyed far too much power to do as it wishes. There are many within the King's inner circle who rail against the body, questioning what many of the representatives' true intentions are. While there are a number of ways they propose to remove this alleged infestation of traitorous elements, this move will represent a radical shift in the balance between the Palace and Sejm.
Safeguard Liberties
While there are many differing political opinions we may find dangerous or harmful, to attack or try to silence them would likely only lead to far greater backlash. It is because of this that more moderate members of the King's inner circle are calling for enshrining fundamental rights to speech and other freedoms in the Kingdom, so that while these dangerous voices may shout, few will have any reason to listen.
Drop the Gold Standard
The Gold Standard has long been part of conventional economic thought with many comforted by the stability seemingly offered by gold backing. For many pro-German interests, it also tied our economy firmly to gold-backed Mitteleuropa. With the crash from Black Monday, the dependence on gold has left our economy unresponsive. In a bid to escape this trap, many within the government are now calling to abandon gold backing and switch to a fully fiat currency.
Float the Złoty
By taking our currency off the Gold Standard, we had to be careful in order to not cause a total currency collapse. Now that some time has been allowed to pass, we can properly reintroduce the Złoty in its new floating form. While this will likely lead to more fluctuating prices, it should hopefully grant us greater means to work our way out of the crisis, while also winning us some support for having a more independent currency from Berlin.
Loans from Foreign Banks
While the crash has made many reluctant to trust the large German and Austrian financial institutions, which they blame for causing the crash, the fact is that these organisations still possess significant capital which can be used to pull us out of the crash. While this move will preserve the status quo of tying us to Berlin and Vienna, it will make it far easier to pull our economy out of this crisis.
Nationalise the Bank of Poland
In the eyes of many, this crash has shown the perils of tying our economy to great powers which will always put their interests above ours. Because of this, many want us to begin pursuing a more independent fiscal policy, something which they believe will help keep us insulated from future instability. This move will not come without consequences however, as it will be a lot harder to raise capital without the vast reserves of Berlin and Vienna.
Pave the Country Roads
The crash has resulted in there being many individuals who are incapable of finding work, which has created a negative feedback loop where they are then unable to spend money, resulting in those who rely on their custom also going under. In a bid to break this cycle, many have proposed getting our unemployed to work in vast public works performing construction, which will have the side benefit of also improving our infrastructure in previously ignored areas.
The Cooperative Movement
Peasant cooperatives have long been a way for poorer rural populations to improve their lot. The combination of providing security and a form of social participation for the rural population have made them a very useful institution to encourage. It is because of this that many are proposing we encourage the creation of new cooperatives which would go a long way to make our food producers secure from market fluctuations.
Marketplace of Mitteleuropa
The trade opportunities present in Poland, thanks to our position between Germany and Austria, should not be so easily discounted. While there are many who propose trying to pull our nation out of the crash by trying to stimulate a domestic economy, the reality is that encouraging a strong export market is a far more proven way to bring cash flowing into our nation. We will begin fostering export markets over domestic ones in order to bring about such conditions.
The Statist Approach
Many would rather sell out our economy to foreign interests in a misguided attempt to bring in more money, ignoring the fundamental issues with placing our fiscal stability at the hands of other nations. If we wish to actually recover from the crash, we must stimulate the economy for our citizens. By encouraging domestic spending and trade, we can restart the fundamentals of our economy, rather than rely on some vague hope of recovery trickling in from Berlin.
The Second Four-Year Plan
While the first four-year plan may not have been a perfect economic policy, the positive effects of the plan are undeniable. Facing another period of industrial and economic decline, many within the government wish to embark on a second plan, hoping to recapture some of the magic of the first. This will set lofty industrial targets for our nation to reach, but should it succeed, it will pave the way for a new prosperous time for Polish industry.
German Investment Plan
Though we may wish to avoid making our economy unnecessarily dependent on foreign capital, the reality is that we will struggle to achieve our industrial targets alone. Therefore, we will begin taking out loans with German banks, with the general aim being that we will be able to easily pay them back through the industrial expansion they will fund.
Rural Literacy Campaigns
Much of our rural population was never able to receive any form of education, and this has gone a long way to entrenching the economic divides and advancement problems in our nation. In a bid to remove the barriers many rural individuals experience due to their lack of education, we will intensify efforts to eliminate rural illiteracy across our nation. While it may prove costly, it is hoped that it will pay off in the long run.
Renovate the University of Warsaw
First established in 1816, the University of Warsaw has had a long tradition of educating the brightest minds in Poland. While this tradition gives it a lot of prestige, a modern centre of education requires far more than status - there are many new fields which require specialised facilities for their exploration, and if we wish to keep our premier educational institution abreast with foreign counterparts, we must invest in its modernisation.
Fuel the Industries
While we have traditionally relied on what's found above the surface for our wealth, many now look eagerly at the potential treasure lying underneath. Not diamonds or gold, but coal. Lots of it. While many of these deposits have been exploited for domestic use, expanding mining operations to a true industrial scale has the potential to transform our nation's economy - providing money not just from the coal itself, but also the many industries that require coal to function.
Expansion of the Electrical Grid
The multitude of benefits from electrification are a matter debated by none. This technology has existed in our cities since the first electric lighting was installed in Warsaw in 1880. While the sector has enjoyed steady growth since then, there are still many in our nation who do not enjoy the benefits of electricity. As part of the modernisation of the economy, many are calling for a focused expansion of electricity across our nation, so that no town will be left in the darkness.
Modernise Urban Infrastructure
Many of our cities are old, and their infrastructure reflects this. A combination of age and underfunding has made our cities seem archaic, with many public services and housing either at their limits or crumbling. A series of ambitious plans have been drafted to completely revitalise Poland's urban areas and their services.
The Central Industrial Region
The flagship of our ambitious industrial programme, the Central Industrial Region will be a concentration of Polish industrial output in the region around Warsaw. This will take advantage of being in the centre of our nation and economy - a beating industrial heart which will represent the transformation of our economy into that of a modern industrial society.
Fund the Construction Sector
While it may sound redundantly obvious, it will be impossible to build an industrial region without the construction services to do so, as we are already finding companies struggling to meet the specifications of modern factories. Funding will be allocated for the expansion and modernisation of construction companies and their equipment. This effort should hopefully allow us to speed up the growth of our industrial capabilities.
War Industry Bureau
While the growing tensions on the continent are bad for peace, they are a good time for arms contractors. In a more pragmatic view, the ability to have a strong arms sector is extremely useful should the nation come to need it. This is the impetus behind the creation of the War Industry Bureau which will oversee the arms manufacturing and logistics sourcing side of the military.
Eastern Europe's Workshop
Looking back on our efforts to build a new crown jewel in our economy, it is almost justified to feel a small sense of pride. We have transformed the area around Warsaw into one of the foremost industrial centres in all of Mitteleuropa, one that is notable in both scale and modernity. While there is still plenty of work left to do, a new golden age for Polish industry is only just beginning.
Expansion of the Consumer Industries
While heavy industry on its own sounds impressive, it is worthwhile to remember that if there is nobody to buy their produce, it is a pointless endeavour. Therefore, we must also make sure that we do not forget to focus on expanding the light consumer goods sector as well. Increasing our population's ability to purchase goods will have the dual benefits of boosting economic growth whilst also hopefully improving the average standard of living.
Stalowa Wola
To further the growth of our new industrial heartland, there has been significant talk of establishing steel works in the region in order to take advantage of the pre-existing coal and iron ore supplies found there. These steelworks, known as Huta Stalowa Wola, will provide thousands of jobs in the region, with plans even being drafted for an entirely planned city to house workers in the plant.
Expand the Chemical Industry
The new and exciting industries of synthetic rubber and fuel production have the potential to be a great boon for nations, such as our own, which struggle to find sufficient supplies of resources. With help from German petrochemical experts, government capital is being directed towards the foundation of new synthetic rubber facilities near the town of Dębica, which will hopefully be the first step in a new economic sector helping to make us more self-reliant.
Domestic Aircraft Manufacturing
The new fields of aviation are seen by many to shape the future of travel and warfare. It is because of this that the next target of government capital is generally seen to be the creation and expansion of a full aviation sector, one which is hoped to be capable of producing domestic aircraft comparable to domestic efforts elsewhere. While reliant on government investment to get off the ground, many hope that these companies will soon be able to soar on their own.
General Inspectorate
Unfortunately the Polish armed forces have been allowed to languish in a state of stagnation for far too long, but as tensions increase across the continent, the will is finally present to fundamentally remake our armed forces. The first step of this will be the creation of a separate body which will oversee its modernisation, hopefully allowing a form of impartiality to prevent any new funding simply increasing officer salaries.
Structural Reorganisations
To begin reforming our armed forces, we must first attack the fundamental structures which make them up. By standardising and updating the administrative and command structures of our military, we can lay the seeds for future growth and expansion, confident that inefficiencies and irregularities have been wiped away.
Malkowski and Malkowska's Legacy
The principles and discipline of scouting, combined with its training of useful skills, like navigating and hiking, are immensely useful for instilling military principles in young children, while also providing them with exciting extracurricular activities. Scouting in Poland was fostered by Olga Małkowska and Andrzej Małkowski, who established institutes to teach scouting principles. By encouraging these organisations, we will foster a generation trained in many useful skills.
Saving Polish Blood
While the willingness of our soldiers to give everything for their country should never be discouraged, we should aim to avoid needless suffering where possible. For any quick heroic death there will be countless slow ones - broken bodies bleeding their life essence into the soil. With timely and trained medical intervention, we can prevent as much of this as possible and get them back to fighting - or at least let one more voice will continue to be heard by their loved ones.
Lessons of the Trenches
The legacy of the trenches haunt society as the enduring image of the Weltkrieg: the mud and cold all worsened by poor construction practices, and a refusal to accept that more permanent fortifications would be necessary. In the future, it will likely be necessary to accept that trenches will play a key part, and by accepting this fact we can hopefully prepare to make our trenches be more bearable and more defensible for those forced to use them.
Obrona Narodowa
The idea of secondary units to support the operations of official troops has been a long standing one, with various militias existing across the world with such a goal in mind. In order to make such a practice more efficient however, many within our military are proposing a state-sponsored volunteer force which will exist to assist the standing army. The name they propose for this organisation is Obrona Narodowa - National Defence.
Mossor's Cavalry Reform
In the west, the role of cavalry units was torn to shreds by machine gun fire: the image of cavalry with sabres charging to their death became a defining notion of the war. In the east however, the wide plains and more fluid nature of warfare has led to cavalry still having a place, but it cannot survive unchanged. Because of this a reform plan has been drafted by one of our commanders, Stefan Mossor, proposing to transform our cavalry into a form of elite mobile infantry.
Equestrian AT Equipment
While many have seen armoured vehicles as the death knell of mounted warfare, the reality is not nearly as simple. The versatility of horses makes them far more able to traverse terrain than vehicles. Proponents of the cavalry force propose expanding this advantage by providing our cavalry with small anti-tank weaponry such as AT rifles, making them able to pierce armour and destroy these vehicles.
Motorised Dragoons
By transporting a cavalry division's equipment by truck and not by horse, the average speed of a unit will increase, and it is able to field more and heavier support weapons, bringing it on par with a normal infantry division's combat power.
Centre for Higher Military Studies
While initiative and natural skill have traditionally been everything good officers needed, the increasingly complex nature of modern warfare will rely on men capable of understanding things which one cannot simply learn on the job. To do this we will establish a new military think-tank capable of enhancing and furthering understanding of modern military tactics and strategy among our officers.
Expand the Academy of Warsaw
The academy at Warsaw is the centre of our officer corps, training many of the junior officers and strategists who shape our military. By pouring increased funding into the body, we can ensure it continues to push out top class graduates. However, is also likely that this modernisation will lead to increased doctrinal squabbling between the various schools of thought. It remains to be seen which will emerge as the orthodoxy.
Combined Arms Warfare
The final years of the Weltkrieg saw a type of warfare far different than what had been seen at the beginning. While men marched across the fields of France, they were no longer the only deciding factor: above them airplanes strafed and fought, artillery behind the lines duelled with greater precision, range and firepower than anything in 1914, while brutish metal beasts lumbered alongside them. This will be how the next war will be fought. We must be ready for it.
Start the Six-Year Plan
While planning to modernise, reform and expand our military is a worthy notion, these plans are little more than fantasies if we do not have the industry to create such a force. Because of this, we will match our programme of military expansion with a parallel programme of expansion in the military industry sector, which other members of the government propose could be tied into broader industrial plans.
Military Research and Education Institute
The advanced equipment required for modern warfare requires genuine innovation and funding to bring into reality: because of this, the government will order the creation of a body to organise military research and to ensure resources are directed towards the right projects. This will also be responsible for assigning funding to projects that would struggle otherwise.
Maroszek's Self-Loading Rifle
An Engineer named Józef Maroszek has come to the new Military Institute with an interesting demonstration: a personal design which he has been refining for a number of years for a rifle which would be far easier to operate than current bolt-action rifles, being capable of firing any time the trigger is pulled (provided it has ammunition of course). This design quickly attracted the support of the Institute and has become one of the first projects approved for further funding.
Artillery Modernisation
Artillery has proven to be one of the greatest deciders of modern war, and the innovation seen during the Great War thoroughly reshaped the field of Artillery research. Twenty years on however, our artillery equipment and training are beginning to seem outdated, and there has been fresh interest in beginning a modernisation of our Artillery Corps, outfitting them with better guns and training them on modern calculations and ranging.
Finish the 8TP Programme
There has been a great deal of exploration and interest in the creation of a Polish tank force, seen as being perfectly suited to the nation's relatively flat geography and tradition for mobile warfare. These efforts have culminated in the 8TP programme, based on the Swedish Landsverk L-60, which will create the first armoured units in a bid to explore how they operate in the field most efficiently.
Project Urugwaj
While we have begun exploring armour technology, we are small fry compared to some of the armoured vehicles seen in other armed forces. This reality has caused us to begin exploring specialised anti-tank weaponry and anti-tank tactics which will allow our infantry and other units to easily slay the metal beasts.
Improved Tank Designs
Our initial experiments into armoured warfare have convinced many to see the advantages in modern warfare, but at the same time the lessons learnt from the experimental units have also shown us the limits of our current armoured vehicles. To overcome this hurdle, fresh funding is being allocated for the design of better armoured vehicles which will be able to go toe-to-toe with foreign counterparts.
Germany's Eastern Bulwark
Bordering the frontier nations in the East and situated closest to Berlin, our nation is in the middle of Germany's order in Eastern Europe. This fact causes us to play a critical role in strategic planning for the entire alliance. By building our nation up as a strong and stable German bastion, we will be able to make ourselves of great use should the need arise while also getting further support from Berlin for our military.
Contracts with CWS
Centralne Warsztaty Samochodowe, created in 1918 to service our army's equipment, has expanded in scale since its humble origins, growing now to be able to produce their own native designs for cars and motorcycles. It stands to reason then that we would support this native company by providing them with lucrative contracts to produce vehicles for our army, strengthening the key bonds between military and industry.
Expand PZInz
Państwowe Zakłady Inżynierii (National Engineering Works) is a company which is fairly experienced in making a wide range of military and civilian vehicles, which are frequently licences of foreign designs. By providing them with funding to expand their operations into the production of domestic armoured vehicles, we will gain access to a relatively stable domestic supplier for our new armoured units.
Develop the 22TP
The earlier 8TP programme has shown the power a more modern tank fleet can have on the battlefield. Looking to expand on this earlier success, plans have been drawn up for the creation of a vehicle which is even larger, better armed and can run more efficiently. This tank has been termed the 22TP by many of its designers, and should we support it, it will truly make our armoured force the envy of the Reichspakt.
Integrated Communication
Our position in the middle of the Reichspakt will make us a key hub of communications, and it is important as part of this that our army is able to work as one and quickly and efficiently communicate with each other. To facilitate this, we will centrally structure our communications system to be standardised and stratified in order to ensure information can gets to who it needs to, when it needs to.
Artillery from the Sky
In the last war, artillery was the nightmare of the common soldier. The idea that at any moment you and everyone in your unit could be wiped out by an enemy you couldn't see is a powerful fear factor. The modern technology of aerial attackers has brought this idea to a new level, with proponents of such warfare pointing to the fact that with proper training, airstrikes can be far more surgical than artillery. This pitch has swayed many in our military, as \
Army-Air-Coordination
While there will always be some resentment between different branches of an armed force, since most soldiers like to believe they have it far worse than their counterparts, it is important not to let these feelings blossom into a full blown inter-service rivalry. While many within the army may see ground units as the only ones that really matter, it is important to make sure that our aerial units work closely with them to maximise their effectiveness.
Mechanisation of the Cavalry
While the cavalry has done an incredible job at keeping their tactics relevant in the rapidly evolving nature of warfare through converting to a sort of mobile infantry, the sad fact is that it is merely holding back the tide. We must make steps to mechanise our cavalry troops to ensure their speed can still remain relevant in the wars of tomorrow.
Centralised Fuel Supply
With the growing mechanisation of our military, it is important that they always have enough fuel to keep them in operation. This has led to calls to create a central organisation to manage the distribution of the fuel supplies of our nation. While this will mostly affect our military through ensuring access to oil, it will also manage other fuel reserves to ensure that they are directed where they need to be.
Wojna Błyskawiczna
The reformation of our military into a mechanised force has led to the creation of a new doctrine of war becoming the orthodoxy — one which relies on speed to win wars. This centres around using a vanguard of armour and airpower to break through enemy forces before using fast-moving motorised infantry to exploit breakthroughs before the enemy can recover. These tactics have even gained a name among our troops, \
Vanguard of the Internationale
The working nation is as uniform as a fighting army. Work is a unifying principle for the nation, just as is war for the army. Polish worker-soldier will act as the spear into the side of Eastern Germany, while the Communards stab the German Eagle in the west.
Art of Operational Planning
Comrade Rokossowski has come home to his nation bringing his theories of Deep Operation. This theory calls for the use of multiple army units all functioning as one. The principle behind these massive operations is that by moving an entire front as one, you destroy enemy units as one on a tactical level. This high-level approach to warfare will take some time to fully implement, but the results it promises will make it worth it.
Strength of Local Initiative
While the crux of deep operations is the strategic level, but that does not mean that the individual tactical level is not also important. As part of this, we must make sure to encourage independent thought in our units in order to ensure any tactical advantages that present themselves are properly exploited by commanders.
Skill of Misdirection
As part of moving our forces as one, it is important that we do not let our enemy realise how they are being manipulated. Instead, we should lead them into the false sense of security that operations are proceeding normally. This misdirection is key to defeating an enemy, blunting his attacks through feigned retreats before overpowering him with a strategic counterpart. We must strengthen our cryptological skills in order to ensure that the enemy cannot decipher our plans.
Spirit of the Hussars
The key to outmanoeuvring an enemy is the ability to be where you want to be, before the enemy can stop this. While traditionally this was done through forcing men to march, modern technology allows us to move faster than any infantryman. By providing our army units with means to reach their objectives quickly, we will ensure they can easily out-manoeuvre their enemies.
Coordination with the Communards
In joining the global revolution, we have become just one part of the great struggle to liberate all of mankind from the shackles of economic slavery. Alone, our cause would be doomed, but by working with our fellow syndicalists, we can act like the twin grips of a vice, slowly crushing the Germans in the middle. In order to ensure this works properly, Internationale diplomats have been noticeably keen to send advisors to oversee the direction of our military and military planning.
Tools for the Shock Troops
In order for our units to break through the enemy and destroy them, they must be properly equipped to crush their opponents. Because of this there has been a strong push to focus our attention on the development of new artillery and infantry equipment, which would hopefully mean that our divisions are able to operate on a far higher level than their opponents.
Eyes from the Sky
While the fight on the ground may seem like the key to deep operations, in reality it is something far more unquantifiable - information. The ability to know how the enemy is moving before he engages is invaluable for planning front movements. Because of this, there has been a great interest in developing technologies to perform reconnaissance of the enemy's movements, both on the ground and in the air.
Concentrated Destruction
The ability for airpower to tear an enemy to shreds is invaluable, as the range and accuracy it can provides leaves artillery severely wanting. In particular the developments in versatile multirole bombers, which can attack both enemy units and strategic targets, are of great interest to military planners as a boon to their operational plans.
Tactical Annihilation
While Deep Operational doctrine typically focuses on the strategic level, it is important to remember what the purpose of those great sweeps of army units is: the complete and utter annihilation of the enemy on a tactical level. By first blunting a more powerful enemy and then crushing him as he is overstretched, we have created a type of war which will make the Germans wish they never marched against the Polish Workers.
Legacy of the Legions
The Polish Legions established during the Weltkrieg have played an important role in the development of the modern Polish state. They had no tanks or planes, only stubborn hearts and an untiring belief in the Polish nation. Technology is useless if the army lacks the spirit to use it, and it is this aspect we should focus on.
National Defence Fund
Military acquisitions are an expensive process, particularly when trying to purchase more modern equipment. The reality is that funding our military modernisation has the potential to bankrupt us. To get around this a proposal has been drafted with support both in government and the army to establish a \
State Aviation Works
The development and production of aviation, vital to our national defence, cannot be left to the fickle hands of private contractors. Because of this, a plan has been established to take aircraft production completely under state management, to ensure that the designs created are completely up to government specifications and army demands.
Domestic Plane Models
While many propose simply producing licences of foreign designs, many within nationalist circles are uncomfortable for the potential this has of leading our aviation development sector into decline. Because of this, there is broad support for looking instead to domestic aircraft designers when producing our aircraft, as while it has to potential to take longer, it will ensure we are not beholden to foreign companies to create our equipment.
Modernisation of Artillery
While our earlier modernisation of artillery units has gone a long way to keeping those units relevant with the rapidly developing pace of warfare, there is always potential to innovate further. New calculation technologies and even higher calibre guns mean that sufficient investment could allow our artillery units to hit the enemy even harder than before.
Motorisation of Cavalry
While we possess some of the most potent cavalry units in the world, unfortunately the writing is on the wall for horses. The potential offered by adopting trucks and cars to transport our troops is simply incomparable. Therefore, by transitioning our cavalry units to using these vehicles instead of their traditional mounts, we will enter them into a new era of their proud history.
Adoption of the 14TP
While the speed of light tanks has often received the most attention from proponents of armour in our nation, many in Rydz-Śmigły's circle now look eagerly towards the fledgling area of the so called \
Moral Education
While many see soldiers as simply a uniform and a weapon, this is far from the truth. Our soldiers serve as representations of our nation's pride and willingness to protect our ideals. They cannot do this if they are not fully appreciative of the ideals they represent when serving. In order to make them never forget their duty, the army command have proposed a healthy nationalist education to be given to all our soldiers in their training process, tying military and patriotism.
National Volunteer Corps
The slow attrition of combat is an unfortunate but inevitable part of modern war. As experienced troops are whittled down by combat, the men replacing them are prone to being less experienced, also weakening morale in the process, as men feel their comrades are being replaced by \
Shield of the Slavic World
With our recent history under the boots of foreign empires, it can be easy to forget our proud history as one of the greatest military powers in Eastern Europe. While we are still not quite at the level of comparative military dominance we once held, we have at least begun to recapture that old spirit. Our troops now march with their heads held high, remembering the reason they fight, the idea they represent, that of a Poland which will never be truly defeated.
Armia Ludowa
Władysław Sikorski is among the men who earned their combat experience in the Polish Legions during the Weltkrieg. Unlike some of his counterparts however, he has an ambitious vision for how the Polish army must operate during the next war. Rather than a conventional armed effort, his plan centres around a massive mobilisation of resources behind the military, pooling state and popular will into one effort to crush the enemy.
Unify the Command Structure
When waging a war with the total military and economic strength of the state behind it, it is vital to ensure that decisions on how to use it are made properly. While some call for simply centralising this control behind a single figure, Sikorski's proposal calls for the creation of bodies under the government capable of directing national resources properly and effectively, which would also prevent the army taking control of politics in such a time of crisis.
Establish a Reserve System
One of the major elements of the popular army concept is the usage of mass mobilisation of the population in the event of conflict. One of the first steps of this will be the establishing of a reserve system to manage and allocate forces effectively should the masses be called upon. This will also keep a list of all potential recruits and their economic necessity to minimise disruption to the logistical side of the military.
Military Self-Sufficiency
When the war comes, it is likely that we will be on our own. If we are to utilise this concept of a massive concentration of state resources properly, we must ensure that our military is not dependent on foreign suppliers for critical equipment. As part of this, there has been a great push to expand the domestic arms sector to produce for any of the key needs of the army.
Professional Core
While mass mobilisation is certainly the most dramatic part of Sikorski's reform plan, it is not the only element. He promotes the idea of a small, specialised core force, envisioning them as motorised and equipped with the best weaponry available. This would make them capable of being the spearhead of any operations, breaking difficult enemy units and filling a role almost comparable to shock troops.
Doctrine of Infantry Tanks
While the showy field of armoured warfare has won many proponents in recent years, this idea of exclusively tank warfare is seen as short sighted under the new vision for the Polish army. While tanks certainly have conditions where they can be useful, their high cost to build and operate makes them far less appealing than a capable infantry unit. To assist this vision, new tank designs are being proposed that rather than acting on their own, would support the infantry in the field.
Air Defence Squadrons
The aerial theatre of operations is core to the plan for a popular army. The first part of this is the creation of a fighter force which is capable of protecting our territory from airborne marauders sent by the enemy, rather than attacking them in their home turf. These fighters will be ready to meet the enemy when they arrive, and deter them from making such forays in the future.
The Bomber Command
Once national airspace has been secured by our fighter aircraft, the real work can begin for our aerial forces - bombing the enemy. This will involve the usage of multirole aircraft capable of attacking both enemy ground targets and key pieces of infrastructure and manufacturing which will cripple their ability to reinforce their troops when our ground forces start their attack.
Polish Citizen-Soldier
As the dividing line between civilian and soldier becomes increasingly blurred under the plans for a popular army, many have been keen to ask where the line actually is? The answer is simple: there is no such line. When the war comes, our citizens and soldiers will become one and the same, as the state itself is transformed into an instrument of war, one where every Pole is part of the fight in some form or another.
The Unshakeable Will
Thanks to Sikorski's reforms, we have succeeded in transforming our military and state into something entirely new. Every citizen of our nation can now feel like a part of the greater engine of national defence, all working to bring about complete and utter victory. When the time comes and we are all called upon, nothing will be left to waste - all will spring to their duty whether that be in the factories or on the frontlines. As one, we are unbreakable.
Election of 1938
The elections of 1938 are shaping up to be rather crucial, with many doubting the ability of the current government to survive in the face of rising opposition to their rule. This ranges from more socialist parties on the left, to staunch conservative forces on the right. It remains to be seen who will have their hands on the tiller when the ballots are counted, but it is certain they will shape Poland to their vision.
Revolutionary Republic
To the surprise of many in the political centre, the monarchy has crumbled and a new Polish Syndicalist Republic has risen from the rubble. The new government is still uncertain and will have to begin rapidly taking steps to entrench itself and begin transforming the old capitalist and German-dominated economy into one that is both socialist and Polish.
Workers' Economy
The economy of a syndicalist state is one which is supposed to be both run and controlled by the workers. For a nation such as ours, which has long been controlled by entrenched interests which worked against the average person, the economy is fundamentally unfair. Therefore, we will begin to create a system where the common workers will control the Polish economy.
Topple the Tyrants
While we have our external tyrants, there are many within our nation as well. From nobility to cruel landowners, much of our nation is controlled by unaccountable local dictators. While many have fled in the wake of the revolution, those that remain will be removed and the structural economic legacy they left will be torn down.
The Myth of the Revolution
As the dust begins to settle, the new Syndicalist nation stands at a crossroads. The coming weeks will force us to make many choices as to the form of our new republic - choices whose legacy will likely cast a shadow on Polish history for years, if not decades to come. A new Poland has been born and it remains to be seen what that will look like.
In Zakrzewski's Light
In the fight for dominance over the soul of the new republic, Zakrzewski's adherents of the committee has come out on top. They reject mere \
Brzozowski-Sorelian Thought
Two main influences behind Zakrzewski's philosophy are Georges Sorel and Stanisław Brzozowski. According to their thinking, the Nation is composed of the workers, and only the workers. Those who leech off the fruits of labour of others are not Poles, but parasites.
Catholic Social Teaching
Catholicism is an integral part of Polish identity, even if the Church is a counter-revolutionary enemy. Through incorporation of Catholic social teaching and worker-priests this link does not need to be severed.
Moral Syndicalism
While syndicalism is traditionally seen as an economic model more than anything else, the writings of Sorel go into far more depth about how such a society should be structured. Syndicalism must include moral rejuvenation of the working class, which must represent the idealised man.
Revolutionary Nationalism
While many see the socialist struggle as an internationalist one between all of the proletariat, reality is far more complicated. As the Italian writer Enrico Corradini proclaimed, there are also 
Piłsudski's Vision
While never a true syndicalist, Józef Piłsudski has become an idol for Zakrzewski and his followers, particularly adapting his ideas of an Intermarium into their goals of liberating Eastern Europe as a whole from its oppressors. To them, issues such as language have little meaning compared to greater class struggle.
The People Must Decide
While the fear of the moment can make it tempting to centralise, to allow the iron fist to direct a nation in a time of crisis would make us no better than our enemies. If we want to show the world who we really are and what we stand for, we must allow the pluralistic side of the committee to flourish, planting the seeds of a democracy by and for the working class.
Chairman Zakrzewski's Dictatorship was averted.
The Supreme Chamber of Commerce
Founded in place of the Senate, the Supreme Chamber of Commerce functions as the syndicalist \
Land of Free Men
Under the old liberal system, there was only freedom for specific groups, who divided the classes into arbitrary groups to keep them weak. Under the new socialist system, all shall enjoy true freedom, the freedom to live and die as equal men, beyond the traditional divides in our society. While instilling this mindset in the average person will be difficult, we will show them how to care.
Peasant Cooperatives
While many look to the trade unionist systems in France and Britain as a model for the new nation, Poland is quite different from either of these examples. Our rural population has led to many proposing instead to encourage the growth of Peasant cooperatives which will be able to collectively elevate Peasant communities and break the traditional mindset of competition which kept them divided.
Healing the Scars
The old order thrived on division. The ability to keep the common man divided from his brothers was key in keeping him trapped in his chains. While we have made steps in waking people from this trance, there are still old grudges which will take more than a few statements to heal. If we can successfully foster further erosion of our traditional divides, we will create a stronger nation.
The French Model
As the two most successful Syndicalist states, it is only natural that they would set the example for future revolutions to follow. The kinks already worked out in Paris and London means that we don't have to figure it out as we go along, and while much of our nation is not as industrial as France or Britain, we can find workarounds for involving our rural population in the process.
Embrace Internationalism
Liberty does not speak one language and does not really represent one nation. While our nations may seem different, in reality our goals are identical - that being the desire for total liberty from oppression and subjugation. Unfortunately, there are still many who labour under oppression, and it is our duty as free peoples to end this gross injustice.
Equality Triumphant
Through our efforts, we have dismantled the systems of unfairness and injustice to their very foundations. The people of our nation now enjoy liberties almost unparalleled in the world, granting them personal, economic and religious freedoms which would have once seemed impossible. Though there is still much work to be done to better the lives of our people, we can know that in a time where many wish to undo freedoms and rights that we stand firm.
Red Intermarium
The peoples of Eastern Europe have long been oppressed by various masters, be they Russian, Austrian or German. The dream of the Intermarium is one which would undo this - the cooperation of the region's peoples which would allow them to stand tall against imperialism. While many dismiss such ideas as unrealistic or idealistic, they once said the same about Syndicalism in Eastern Europe, and they will be proven wrong again.
Polish Socialist Republic
We must admit the facts - even if we incorporate our smaller neighbouring peoples into our nation with good intentions, we will be seen as the conquerors. A government that drags the Polish people into a war has already abandoned its primary duty - to improve the lives of the Poles.
Central European Confederation
What truly united the Commonwealth of old were shared interests and loyalty: a desire to build a better tomorrow for everyone instead of mindless conquest that would only bring bloodshed. It is this path of cooperation that we must strive for if we are to see the old days of glory return.
Ascension of the Centrolew
In a grim turn for the pro-German elements in our nation, the Centrolew bloc has managed to secure a victory in the election. Falling to the left politically and economically, these parties envision an ambitious series of reforms to break up the status quo and strengthen democratic control over the nation's political direction. Their plans are also likely to involve further decoupling of Poland from the German economic hegemony and working closer with their brothers in Galicia.
§SThe Centrolew government decreases the possibility of a socialist revolution massively.§!
Embrace Secularism
Key to the goal of a Poland which works for all her citizens is enshrining a nation where they will not be judged by their creed. To ensure that the state cannot be used to disadvantage those of other faiths, a wedge will be driven firmly between it and the church. While we have no issue with being religious in private, these are two spheres that should not interact, no matter what some in politics may demand.
Free and Secular Education
The youth represent the future of our nation, and while education in our nation has made incredible advances in recent years, there are still many who miss out because of economic or geographic circumstances. In a bid to rectify this failing, it has been proposed to offer free education to all who want it, using a curriculum which would be centrally managed to ensure all students are taught the same knowledge.
Enshrine Minority Rights
For the various religious and cultural minorities of Poland, the election of a new government does little to give them hope that discrimination against them will end, just because the current people in power are opposed to it. To prevent any progress we make in healing archaic divisions being undone by our successors, we will make steps to enshrine the rights of minorities in law.
Female Suffrage
The idea of womens' suffrage has spread rapidly across the world in recent decades, as women began to end their silence and demand equal rights to men. Through their activism they have managed to secure major victories in their struggle, with many nations in Europe granting women the right to vote. With more radical individuals in power, these calls finally have a voice in government: the time has come for Poland to join the liberal nations of the world and let women have their say.
Shackle the Senate
The upper house of the Sejm has proven itself to be the citadel of conservatism and reactionary thought, allying itself with the Germans rather than with the people of Poland. This archaic institution has one purpose: to slow down progress. In our ideal Poland such an elitist body would not exist, but for time being we can only reduce their influence in favour of the lower house.
Curtail the Geheimrat
The King's Privy Council is the very embodiment of unelected elites controlling the nation instead of the people of Poland. One way to restrict their influence is to curtail the membership to only true citizens of Poland, which would greatly reduce German influence over us.
Land of the Peasants
The majority of our nation belong to the class of relatively poor peasants who work hard and receive little thanks for their labour. Campaigning on a platform of expanding democracy and reforming archaic institutions, many within the government wish to centre programmes around making this nation one which is made by and works for the peasants via popular land reforms and attempting to better their economic prospects.
Create the Chamber of Labour
Believing the nascent urban working class to be the future of the Polish economy, there are many within the more urban cohort of our government who believe working to better their conditions should be core to our reforms. One of their first ideas to do this is to create a \
Nationalise the Vital Sectors
While we do not entirely reject the free market like the far more radical syndicalists do, there are strong voices within our administration who believe that the government is the best to provide what they term \
Creation of Small Farms
There are many problems with the current distribution of land in our rural areas, and while many propose more cautious reform, such a programme would not do enough to eliminate the roots of the problem. Rather, many believe that a more total redistribution of the land is needed to create a fairer situation for peasants, taking it from those who own the land and giving it to those who actually use it.
Secure Workers' Rights
It is a fact of life that people need to work in order to have a comfortable life, a fact that gives employers an unfair degree of power over the conditions that they can demand their workers to be forced to endure. This is an area where the state actually has immense power to do good, using its sheer power to compel employers to display a minimum level of care towards their workers. This should hopefully limit accidents and deaths in our industrial sector.
National Healthcare
Medicine has made great strides in recent years, but unfortunately these developments do not reach all equally with disadvantages in areas often being unable to get equal treatment with the wealthy. Nobody should die simply because they were unable to afford healthcare or were unable to access it. The government will provide healthcare to all in our nation - a basic good to make our citizens' lives infinitely better.
Unionisation of the Peasants
While most think of unions as representing the interests of workers in grimy factories, farmers are just as capable of working together to represent their interests. To help our rural areas transition to a more representative system for their sector of the economy, the government will support the creation of unions for our peasants and farmers. After all, if they go on strike, who will provide the food the rich need to survive?
Union with Kraków
Kraków, the old royal capital of Poland, lies just beyond our border along with the rest of Galicia. This origin of the partition is entirely artificial, enforced by Austrians and Germans rather than Poles. With the election of a more liberal government, there have been increased calls to unite with the region which has long been a shelter for democrats and republicans. This will not be easy, as any such union relies on the consent of Berlin and Vienna.
The Austro-Hungarian Empire is §Rnot§! in civil war.
Nationalise the Infrastructure
Trains, roads and ports are all key parts of our nation's transport infrastructure. In spite of this importance, much of their maintenance is left to a chaotic myriad of groups, which has produced less than stellar results. It would be better for the state to step in and take direct management of key infrastructure in order to ensure resources are being directed for the greatest return for the people.
Thorough Land Reform
Land reform has been the key economic and social question for our nation, and it is one our government must attempt to solve as part of our more peasant-focused reforms. Our plan envisions a careful but comprehensive reform of land usage within our nation, which will allow many to actually access the land which they work so hard to make productive.
People's Banks
For many in our nation, access to loans and capital vital to improve their economic situation is very hard to come by. The reality is that many financial institutions are unwilling to lend to peasants. In a novel idea to solve this problem, the government has proposed a system of communal banking where members of a community would all contribute, and from which loans could be better provided, hopefully allowing greater access to cheap credit.
Democracy and Transparency
Democracy is not just something which can be enacted in laws, it is something which must be built up in the minds of the population. By making them think democratically, understanding and respecting civil and political liberties as core parts of their lives, they will be able to foster our democratic system into something which can exist organically with full consent from the people.
Unicameralism
While many liberal democracies operate on a bicameral system where a lower house must cooperate with an upper house of some form, this system serves as an extra degree of separation of the people from their government - something which is anathema to our beliefs. Therefore we will empower a single legislative body to make decisions in our nation, ensuring a direct line between voters and the policies of the government.
Sincere People's Government
A government must be more than simply a set of policies or men in offices - it is supposed to embody the beliefs of the majority and work for the people. While some may call it idealism, arguing that no democratic system can withstand the realities of governance, we will strive to prove them wrong by creating a government which works by and for the people.
The Dawn of Progress
Thanks to our efforts, we have totally overhauled the political and social makeup of Poland while not wholly abandoning the things which make us unique. Democracy is not always the most inspiring ideology and is frequently attacked by those seeking to make it seemed flawed, but we have shown that idealism still has its place. A new Poland has been created - a model for other democracies to follow.
His Majesty's Cabinet
Despite the determined attempts of the opposition, the Pro-German Circle has come out on top in the election. With their victory, it is likely that the ideas of strong, stable government will continue in the future, with the Circle attempting to strengthen the centre against increasingly powerful fringes and a careful reform of government institutions along the Circle's principles.
Empower the Geheimrat
The election was a concerning time for many of the more actively pro-German members of the King's inner circle, with genuine concerns of the opposition taking power. Now that their position has been confirmed for now, many are now pushing to strengthen their bonds with the King to ensure that the correct voices advise him on policy in the future.
Entrenched Constitutionalism
While we have significant disagreements with the more radical Centrolew, we do share their belief in reform of the legislative system, providing more power to the Sejm and putting these bodies in a more equal balance with the King. This will hopefully also win us support from more moderate Centrolew supporters who will support moderate reform over none at all.
Ally the Szlachta
As the party representing a more stable balance between expanding native representation and preserving the key institutions of our society, we are in a great position to align ourselves with more liberal members of the nobility. Their support will allow us to make inroads in rural areas while also hopefully winning us some concessions when the time comes to answer the question of land reform.
Fill the Railway Gaps
Our legacy as a mere province has left us with a rather chaotic rail network, with a lack of connections between our internal system and that of our neighbours. This hampers our ability to transport by rail and benefit from our very central location in the Reichspakt, with many routes simply going around Poland even if it adds extra distance to their journey. Solving this lack of connection could provide us with a lot of benefits economically and logistically.
Friends in Vienna
For many within Centrolew, Austria represents a far more comfortable middle ground as a trade partner, both thanks to being a traditional shelter for democrats, and also because it would not result in us becoming further tied to Berlin. With the pre-existing economic connections to Galicia, encouraging economic ties between us and Vienna would be in the interests of both nations.
Allies in Lewiatan
In an effort to avoid ceding any more economic leverage to Berlin, a group of Polish industrialists known as \
The Constitutionalist Coalition
A truce has been made between the republicans and the monarchy. United in defence of Polish democracy, the moderates of both sides have agreed to form a surprise coalition to stem the radicalism from both sides, trying to maintain a careful balancing act.
Allies in Berlin
As the largest source of foreign investment in our economy, it is only natural that we should seek to further develop our ties with Germany. While some claim that this makes us more liable to suffer should the German economy experience spirals, they fail to argue how a Polish economy would be immune to such a crash. In addition, by proving ourselves to be such a reliable partner to Berlin, we will likely have a lot of persuasion from German business interests to stay that way.
Attract German Corporations
Thanks to our efforts to prove ourselves as a reliable investment location, we have received a lot of interest from large German conglomerates looking either to establish new operations, or expand already existing ones. These companies have the potential to provide a lot of indirect benefits to our economy, provided we can convince them to follow on from these probing inquiries.
Rule by Royal Decree
In issues of national concern, it is not useful nor \
Guarded Democracy
While democracy is a good on principle, not every man is mature and good enough to be trusted with decisions regarding their country. As Roman Dmowski often said, the Commonwealth of old squandered its might in democratic bickering and plotting. We must ensure that the Sejm will always stay on the right path, regardless of communist agitators and others who would see Poland subjugated again.
Unite the Poles
With Germany making indications that they are willing to move beyond the status quo that has prevailed since their victory in the Weltkrieg, many have proposed to lobby Berlin on the issue of Polish unity, specifically around Galicia. Should this proposal be accepted, it would represent a major change in the situation of all Poles and be a huge victory for our government.
Primacy of the Sejm
It is impossible for one man to rule alone, and the Sejm has already prove itself to be more than capable of handling some duties as loyal servants of the King. This delegation has continued to the point where the Sejm has functionally become the controlling body of government, and there are those proposing we formalise this relationship, while at the same time making it clear they will still work with powers bestowed by their Monarch.
Manage the Unions
While few dispute that Unions can play an important role in society, their noble idea is very liable to being infiltrated by elements which claim to represent the interests of the workers. In order to prevent our unions becoming corrupted, the government will mandate government-appointed officials be placed in key union positions, while at the same time having plants within the unions to cut out the rot before it can spread.
Royal Academy of Arts
It is important that the people remember that the King is their King, and cares about their culture and history. In an effort to demonstrate this fact, plans have been drafted to create a royal institution to foster the Arts, which will demonstrate the King's willingness to support Polish culture and arts.
In the Middle of Mitteleuropa
The Central Industrial Region, our new economic core, also has the potential to be an economic hub for the entirety of Mitteleuropa. By strengthening rail and industrial links between the Region and the rest of Eastern Europe, we have the potential to have a nexus of the entire half of the continent in our hands, on par with any of the great cities of Europe.
Secure the Magnates
The large estates of our nation serve as a key part of safeguarding Polish economic interests, in spite of their inefficiencies. While majority Polish, there are great estates controlled and populated by those who are not Poles. These estates have few friends and are often hated by Polish landowners due to claims of undercutting. To get these Magnates on our side, we will begin dismantling these non-Polish strongholds and transform them into proper Polish communities.
Abolish the Royal Veto
With the status of the Sejm as the primary governing force entrenched, there have been growing calls to abolish the ability for the King to veto any legislation he sees fit. Many criticise this both for the pure undemocratic nature of it, and because it makes little sense given the King has given up most of his other powers. With the agreement of the Palace, the government will finally abolish the veto and make the Sejm the sole law-making body in Poland.
The Path of Least Resistance
Through the efforts of the Circle, Polish politics have been reformed at a slow but steady place. A new balance between the King and the people has been struck, showing that monarchies are more than capable at adapting to changing circumstances around them. With the threats to the further left and right now on the backfoot thanks to decisive action, the centre has triumphed in Poland - an island of stability in stormy seas.
Christian Conservatism
With the rise of the more right-wing and nationalist elements of Polish politics, culminating in their recent seizure of power, Polish politics are likely to see a rapid shift towards a more traditional style of governance. The new government generally focuses on intertwining Polish nationalist beliefs, with the traditional dominance held by the Catholic Church in the nation, arguing the strength of one is directly proportional to the other.
§cEven as a monarchy, nationalist Poland will not necessarily be loyal to Germany.§!
Cement the Church's Status
In one of the first moves of the new government to entrench its ideals, plans are being drafted to recognise the Catholic Church as the state religion of Poland. They argue that by formalising the status quo, they will recognise the important role the Church has played in preserving our Nation's spirit. While this is supported by many Catholics, it is looked upon fearfully by religious minorities, fearing it may entrench pre-existing discrimination by providing legal legitimacy.
Purge the Nationalist Terrorists
The nationalist elements within our nation are nothing but a danger, managing to convince Poles that opposing the rule of law is somehow in their best interests. This dangerous thought threatens to spread if not swiftly removed, lest it corrupt the entire nation. Eliminating these radical nationalists will help in moderating the discussion of independence, while hopefully removing a potential threat.
Outlaw the Austrian Agents
While there are many within our nation campaigning for some degree of separation from the Germans, not all of these have entirely pure motivations. Concern has been raised due to representatives who come from the Austrian Empire to the south. While these individuals claim to be entirely independent, their reliance on Galicia has not gone unnoticed - because of this, there are many who have begun calling to act on these potential saboteurs before they can undermine us.
Arrest the Socialist Agitators
The radicals of the left make big claims, ceaselessly ranting about the injustices of capitalism and what they claim is a positively feudal system. Worryingly, this talk appears rather popular among our lower classes, who seem to believe the idealistic portrayal of the Syndicalist societies in the West. It is important that we crack down on this talk quickly, before it can get even more out of control.
Christian Trade Unionism
The rabid preachers of the left like to place themselves as the sole representatives of workers' rights, a convenient brush to paint their opponents with. In reality, valuing human dignity and fairness are far more connected with the teachings of Christ than those of any intellectual. To prevent the corruption of our workers, we will encourage the creation of unions based on papal ideas - a system of neither capitalism nor syndicalism which will protect Catholic values.
Eliminate Class Divisions
The petty divisions of class are entirely arbitrary and pointless, created by others to divide one Pole from another. It doesn't take a syndicalist to see that this is not right. In our new Poland, we must work to erode and eventually destroy these divisions - a move which will both unite and strengthen our people, being able to work as one to counter their enemies abroad which would seek to exploit these divisions.
The Christian Coalition
Despite our disagreements with the Germans, they were right in one matter: monarchy is the natural social order of any Christian nation, and therefore the Polish Catholics should seek not to oppose, but to glorify the monarchy and its stand against godless socialism.
Reinforce the Parliamentary System
While our current parliamentary system has a lot of serious issues in the eyes of many in government, the more pragmatic can see the clear benefits of working through this flawed structure to provide our decisions with a much greater degree of legitimacy. Fostering a strong parliamentary system will also have the benefit of making the people feel truly engaged with our policies, giving them a more bottom-up feeling of power.
Slay the Hydra of Capitalism
Recent decades have seen multinational capitalist systems dominating the global order. These structures, sold as positive and equal, in reality serve to exploit the weakest peoples and nations by pre-existing controllers. If we do not reverse this course, we will all be subordinate to foreign markets, and our nation's will would effectively be nullified. Despite the challenges, we must fight against this hegemony, so our nation will stand when the markets bring all others tumbling down.
First Marshal of Poland
Edward Rydz-Śmigły has taken up the mantle of Marshal of Poland, the supreme leader and protector of the nation. He has carefully fostered this aura around himself of being an embodiment of the Polish nation, commanding it as he would any military unit. Now at the helm of the nation, his policies will likely focus on entrenching this image and correcting the \
The Party of National Unification
The challenges facing our state require a united political front against our enemies: the petty divisions of conventional politics simply distract and undermine our struggle. We must further strengthen the image of the OZN as a party which all Poles must support. Campaigns will be mounted against those who attempt to denigrate and attack the noble aims of our party. Their gossip will not be tolerated.
Centralisation of Power
Despite our efforts to counter division and squabbling, many refuse to keep with the programme. It has become clear that the people cannot be relied on to act in their best interests. We must demonstrate to them that the united and uncompromising state, guided firmly by its leader, is the only way to bring Poland into a brighter tomorrow. Through intense propaganda efforts and a regulation of dangerous thought, we will make this united nation a reality.
The Saviour of Poland
Thanks to the efforts of Rydz-Śmigły, the enemies of the Polish people are slowly being driven out. The regime has been building up the image of the Marshal as a guiding hand, taking the reins of a nation heading to ruin, and setting us back on the right course. It is important the people of Poland never forget this deed, and new laws are being proposed which would require portraits to be placed in all public buildings across the nation. A small thanks for his noble effort.
Corporatism
The economic and social sectors have long been framed as being pitted against each other, all competing for resources and money. This destructive child of Liberalism serves to do nothing but breed division and discontent. In the new Poland, a more harmonious economic model is envisioned, modelled on the principles of corporatism. Rather than competing, the separate economic sectors will be mandated to work in tandem, like the individual organs of the creature that is the economy.
Social Altruism
Through the previous damage of the free market, many have managed to slip below the cracks and now live in abject poverty. Embracing the Christian ethos of charity and alms-giving, we will aim to alleviate their suffering, providing them with the basic requirements needed to live life as God wished them to. This goodness should hopefully make the lives of the poor better, while also show it is not godless syndicalists who value the lives of the unfortunate, but all good Christians.
Managed Land Reform
While solving the issue of unequal land distribution is obviously one which must be solved to allow our people to prosper, we must be careful to not capsize the boat when trying to change tack. Any radical action like that envisioned by other reformers would only alienate landowners and do greater damage in the long run. Therefore, we must engage in careful and fair distribution of land assets, properly compensating any who lose their property.
Polonisation Programmes
It is unfair that in a nation of Poles, it is often those not of native blood that control significant amounts of our nation. These minorities keep to themselves, extracting wealth from our nation and people. We must take firm action to eliminate these groups, either through integration into Polish culture or through a destruction of their power and social cliques. After all, there are already nations for Germans or Ukrainians: Poland should be for the Poles.
The First of the Slavs
While we are obviously firmly committed to the ideals of liberty for all Slavs, we cannot let such a cause come at the expense of our own nation's right to prosper. We must work to create the ideal Polish nation before we go about trying to assist in the liberation of our Eastern brothers, some of whom directly oppose the goals of a strong and defendable Poland. Once our people are reunited again under our banner, the Polish eagle will soar high across the East once again.
True Catholic [POL.GetKingdomOrRepublicCap]
Through our efforts, we have turned the Church from something increasingly marginalised into a core pillar of our state. Across the nation, our people slowly rediscover not just their patriotism, but their faith. The strong ties between Rome and Warsaw will never be broken, and we can only hope that his Holiness will be willing to return our faithfulness in the future. A brighter, more moral future is about to begin for the true sons and daughters of Poland.
The Exceptional Individual
According to Adam Doboszyński, every generation has their exceptional individuals, and those persons must take a guiding role in completely reforging the Polish national identity into one which does not strongly connect to the Church, but actively implements their ideas for social, political and economic organisation.

In the first steps of our new state, we must eliminate these elements if we wish to succeed in our mission to transform the Polish nation. While this move will likely be very unpopular, it will likely break the power of religious minorities to ignore the word of God.
